<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="case-management-under-order-11">CASE MANAGEMENT UNDER ORDER 11<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#case-management-under-order-11" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Pre-trial procedure is simply a conference between opposing counsel, conducted under the supervision and guidance of the court, for the purpose of crystallizing issues, eliminating matters that are not actually in controversy, and stipulating as many facts as can be agreed upon.</p>
<ul>
<li>The pre-trial procedure is spread across three separate pre-trial conferences, namely:</li>
</ul>
<p>(1) case conference under Order 11 Rule 3;</p>
<p>(2) settlement conference under Order 11 Rule 5, and;</p>
<p>(3) trial conference under Order 11 Rule 7,</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="application">Application<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#application" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This Order shall apply to all suits except small claims as defined under O.3(1) or such other suits as the court may by order exempt from this requirement (r.1)</li>
<li>The aim is to deal with preliminary issues well in advance so that the trial once commenced must proceed on a day to day basis without unnecessary interruptions</li>
<li>Time allocation is dealt with at this stage.</li>
</ul>
<p>With a view to furthering expeditious disposal of cases and case management the court shall within 30days after the close of pleadings convene a Case Conference in which it shall deal with the issues laid out in r.3 (1) (a-i) (r.3(1))</p>
<ul>
<li>In addition to any other general power, the court may also case conference on matters arising under r.3(2) (a-o)</li>
</ul>
<p>011 r3. (1)</p>
<p>(a) consider compliance with Order 3 rule 2 and Order 7 rule 5;</p>
<p>(b) identify contested and uncontested issues;</p>
<p>(c) explore methods to resolve the contested issues;</p>
<p>(d) where possible secure parties’ agreement on a specific schedule of events in the proceedings;</p>
<p>(e) narrow or resolve outstanding issues;</p>
<p>(f) create a timetable for the proceedings;</p>
<p>(g) change the track of a case;</p>
<p>(h) consider consolidation of suits;</p>
<p>(i) identify a test suit and order stay of other suits</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="011-r3-2">011 r3(2)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#011-r3-2" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>(a) deal with any interlocutory applications or create a suitable timetable for their expeditious disposal;</p>
<p>(b) order the filing and service of any necessary particulars within a specific period;</p>
<p>(c) order admission of statements without calling for the makers as witnesses where appropriate and the production of any copy of a statement where the original is unavailable;</p>
<p>(d) order the giving of evidence on the basis of affidavit evidence or give orders for discovery or production or inspection or interrogatories which may be appropriate to the case;</p>
<p>(e) order for the examination of any witness by an examiner or by the issue of Commission outside court and for the admission of any such examination as evidence in court;</p>
<p>(f) make any procedural order;</p>
<p>(h) make a referral order for alternative dispute resolution;</p>
<p>(i) convene a hearing;</p>
<p>(j) give any suitable directions to facilitate expeditious disposal of the suit or any outstanding issues;</p>
<p>(k) encourage the parties to co-operate with each other in the conduct of the proceedings;</p>
<p>(l) help the parties to settle the whole or part of the case;</p>
<p>(m) consider whether the likely benefits of taking a particular step justifies the cost of taking it;</p>
<p>(n) deal with as many aspects of the case as it can on the same occasion;</p>
<p>(o) make any such orders as may be appropriate including—</p>
<p>(i) striking out the action or defence;</p>
<p>(ii) making an award of costs;</p>
<p>(iii) striking out of any document or part of it; or</p>
<p>(iv) creating or amending a case timetable</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="timetable-of-the-case-conferencing">Timetable of the case conferencing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#timetable-of-the-case-conferencing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Once pleadings are closed under Order 2 rule 13, the parties are supposed to complete, file and serve within 10 days a Pre-trial Questionnaire appearing in Appendix B (r.2)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Within 30 days after close of the pleadings the court convenes a Case Conference. Parties are expected to make sure that they have filed in the pre-trial questionnaire before the court convenes a Case Conference (r.3)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>After the Case Conference, Case Conference Order in terms of Appendix C is made (r.4)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Within 60 days of Case Conference in case of fast track cases and 90 days in multi-track cases, the court convenes a Settlement Conference. This is meant to explore avenues for settlement or narrowing down the issues (r.5(1))</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>7 days before the settlement conference, parties are to prepare and exchange a Settlement Conference Brief which contains summary of the facts including issues and admissions, summary of the law to be relied upon, final list of witnesses and statements and expert reports and relevant portions of the documents to be relied upon (r.5(2))</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>30 days before the hearing, a Trial Conference is to be convened by the court to plan trial time, explore expeditious ways of introducing evidence, amend pleadings, deal with admissions, allow adduction of affidavit evidence, make orders for commissions, expert evidence, ADR etc. At the end of Trial Conference the parties sign a Trial Conference Memorandum in Appendix E and the court proceeds to make orders necessary for the conduct of the suit (r.7)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The Parties are bound by the memorandum signed herein unless the court decides otherwise (r.8)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>R.7(2) imposes a duty on every party and or his advocate to strictly comply with the provisions of r.3(2) and to give such information as the judge may require, including but not limited to the number of the witnesses expected to be called and the nature of their evidence, to enable the court to consider and settle the length of time which will probably be required for the hearing of the suit.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Any wilful failure or omission of compliance of any of the provisions under r.7 is deemed to be a violation of the overriding objective as stipulated in Section 1A and 1B of the Act and the court may order costs against the defaulting party unless for reasons to be recorded, the court orders otherwise</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In the meantime and at least 10 days before the trial parties were expected to have completed, filed and exchanged Trial Conference Questionnaire Form in Appendix D (r.6)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To implement this order the Chief Justice is empowered to appoint Case Management Judges and Case Managers as he deems necessary (r.9)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>NOTE: That the failure to adhere to the provisions of this order may invite sanctions and penalties.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="discovery">Discovery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#discovery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Discovery is available in civil cases as provided for in the Civil Procedure Rules.</li>
<li>Order 11, Rule 3 (2) states that the court may order that evidence be given on the basis of affidavit evidence or give orders for discovery or production or inspection or interrogatories which may be appropriate to the case.</li>
<li>A party may serve a Notice of Examination on an opposing party, indicating a time and place where the party must attend to answer questions under oath. The examination is recorded, and where requested, transcribed.</li>
<li>There are two types of discovery, which are Discovery of Facts and Discovery of Documents.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="discovery-of-facts">Discovery of Facts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#discovery-of-facts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>This is done by way of interrogatories (meaning to question or enquire) and can only be issued with leave of court.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The purpose of interrogatories is to know the nature of the case of the opponent and to elicit facts that support your own case – you can do it directly by obtaining admissions or by impeaching or destroying the case of the opponent.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The general rule is that the court will always allow interrogatories that will assist in the administration and dispensation of justice and also those that will shorten litigation, reduce costs and save time.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The court will also only allow interrogatories that are relevant to the matters in issue.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Interrogatories will not be allowed if they seek facts which are confidential, are injurious to public safety and security, are scandalous, irrelevant or lack bona fides, are based on questions of law, are administered unreasonably, or are vexatious and oppressive.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="discovery-of-documents">Discovery of Documents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#discovery-of-documents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>This is done to secure as far as possible the disclosure on oath of all material documents in the possession or power of the opposite party and to put an end to what might otherwise lead to a protracted inquiry as to the material documents actually in the possession or power of the opposite party.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The general rules relating to discovery are that it should be voluntary and automatic in that you do not need the leave of court to issue discoveries until the other party</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>There are, however, limits to discovery, as privileged information is not subject to the process.</p>
<ul>
<li>A party can apply to the court to cross-examine any person who has put in any affidavit evidence in order to obtain more information that one feels is within the knowledge of the party to be examined.</li>
<li>Discovery is administered by the litigants but under the court’s direction, and hence the parties must agree on a discovery plan if they wish to obtain evidence through the discovery process.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="legal-privilege">Legal Privilege<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#legal-privilege" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The Republic of Kenya recognises the concept of legal privilege.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Advocates are under a duty to keep confidential the affairs of their clients, and the circumstances in which they are able to disclose client communications are strictly limited.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Section 134(1) Evidence Act provides that an advocate shall not disclose communication made to them by their client nor disclose documents provided by clients or legal advice given to the client; it is a professional privilege.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>However, there is an exception when it comes to matters of illegal acts.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If a client communicates with an advocate in furtherance of illegal acts, then the advocate is under a duty to disclose such facts.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There is no distinction between external and internal counsel where privileged information is concerned.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There is no exemption to privileged information and an advocate must uphold this duty at all times.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>LECTURE 17: HEARING AND CONSEQUENCES OF NON-ATTENDANCE</p>
<p>ISSUES RELATING TO NON-ATTENDANCE AT TRIAL 0.12</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="non-attendance-by-parties-or-non-attendance-of-either-party">Non-attendance by parties or non-attendance of either party<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#non-attendance-by-parties-or-non-attendance-of-either-party" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>When neither party attends, the court may dismiss the suit (r.1)</li>
<li>When only the plaintiff attends –</li>
<li>(a) if notice of hearing was duly served, it may proceed ex parte</li>
<li>(b) if that notice of hearing was not duly served, it shall direct a second notice to be served, or</li>
<li>(c) if notice was not served within sufficient time or for sufficient reason the defendant was unable to attend, it may postpone hearing (r.2)</li>
</ul>
<p>If on the day of the hearing, only the defendant attends and he denies the claim, the suit shall be dismissed unless good cause is shown which should be recorded in court</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>If the defendant admits any part of the claim the court shall give judgment against the defendant upon such admissions and shall dismiss the suit so far as relates to the rest of the claim except for good cause to be recorded in court</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the defendant counterclaims he may proof his counterclaim so far as the burden of proof lies on him (r.3)</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="effect-of-dismissal">Effect of dismissal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effect-of-dismissal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>If only some of the plaintiff’s attend, the court may either proceed with the suit or make such orders as it may deem just (r.4).</li>
<li>If only some of the defendants attend, the court may proceed with the suit and may give such judgment as is just in respect of the defendants who have not attended (r.5).</li>
<li>Subject to r.2 and any law of limitation of actions, where a suit is dismissed under this Order the plaintiff may bring a fresh suit</li>
<li>However, when a suit is dismissed under r.3, no fresh suit may be brought in respect of the same cause of action (r.6).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="setting-aside-judgment-or-dismissal">Setting aside judgment or dismissal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#setting-aside-judgment-or-dismissal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Where under this Order judgment has been entered or suit has been dismissed, the court may on application set aside or vary the judgment or order upon such terms as may be just (r.7).</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Other circumstances under which a suit may be dismissed before trial include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Dismissal for want of prosecution under Order 17 of the Civil Procedure Rules in a suit where no step has been taken for the period of one year;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dismissal for failure to give security for costs under Order 26;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Failure to collect Summons or having failed to serve the Summons, the suit then abates (Order 5);</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Withdrawal/discontinuance and adjustment of the suit by the plaintiff;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Out-of-court settlements; or</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Other preliminary objections.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>LECTURE 18: THE PARTIES' DAY IN COURT</p>
<p>TRIAL STAGE</p>
<p>At the hearing, the parties may appear before court in person or by an advocate or recognised agent.</p>
<ul>
<li>The trial starts with opening statements from the advocates of the parties.</li>
<li>The plaintiff shall have the right to begin.</li>
<li>Unless:</li>
</ul>
<p>(i) a preliminary objection has been filed, or</p>
<p>(ii) where the defendant admits the facts alleged, or contends a point of law or,</p>
<p>(iii) based on additional facts, the plaintiff is not entitled to any of the reliefs sought, or</p>
<p>(iv) when the court otherwise orders.</p>
<p>The party having the right to begin will call their witnesses one by one until the last witness.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The witnesses are examined in-chief, cross-examined and re-examined.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The litigant or the advocate then makes a final speech, so closing their case.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Time limits are at the discretion of the court.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>After the close of the plaintiff’s case, the defendant states their case.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the defendant elects to give evidence, the defendant’s case is opened and the defendant’s witnesses are called, examined in-chief, cross-examined by the other party and finally re-examined, if need be, until the last witness testifies.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A closing speech is made for the defendant, followed by the closing speech for the plaintiff.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The closing speeches may be in the form of oral or written submissions, as the court may permit.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The parties may with leave of the court choose to highlight their written submissions or adopt the submissions as they are.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The court will then fix a date when the judgment will be pronounced in court.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="evidence">Evidence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#evidence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The rules governing the admission or admissibility of evidence at trial are found under Part II of the Evidence Act (Cap. 80), the Civil Procedure Act (Cap. 21) and the Civil Procedure Rules.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Section 5 of the Evidence Act provides that no evidence shall be given in any suit or proceeding except evidence of the existence or non-existence of a fact in issue and of any other fact declared by any provision of the Act to be relevant.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Part I of the Evidence Act provides for the admissibility and relevancy of evidence in a trial.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Part II, on the other hand, provides for admissions by parties to the suit and the effects of admission as evidence in a trial.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Admissions, however, are not conclusive proof of the matters admitted but they may operate as an estoppel.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Evidence in a trial can be either oral or documentary evidence.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All facts except the contents of the documents may be proved by oral evidence.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Oral evidence must be direct.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Documentary evidence may be either primary or secondary evidence.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>As a general rule, documents must be proved by primary evidence except where primary evidence may not be obtained without unreasonable delay when secondary evidence may be adduced to prove the existence of the original.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The rule of admission of evidence lies with the principle that he who alleges must prove.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The person adducing evidence must lay a foundation and prove its existence for the evidence to be admitted at trial.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="expert-testimony">Expert Testimony<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expert-testimony" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Expert testimony is permitted at trial.</li>
<li>When a court has to form an opinion upon a point of foreign law, or on science or art, or to identify the authenticity of handwriting or fingerprints or other impressions, opinions upon that point are permissible if made by persons specially skilled in such foreign law, science or art, or in questions as to identity or genuineness of handwriting or fingerprints or other impressions.</li>
</ul>
<p>Under Order 11, Rule 5(2), parties to a suit are required to prepare and exchange a Settlement Conference Brief which should include and is not limited to expert reports and the relevant portions of documents relied upon.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It therefore means that either party can introduce their individual experts, but if there is a dispute as to the reliability of an expert witness, the court will settle for a neutral expert to testify in court.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Under Section 48 of the Evidence Act, where the court has to form its opinion on a particular matter, the court may seek the opinion of persons specially skilled in that area known as “experts”.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>In the case of <em>Nyaribo Nyankomba v. Mary Bonarere Munge [2010] eKLR</em>, it was held that in customary law cases, it is necessary for experts versed in the particular customs be summoned to testify so as to assist the court in reaching a fair verdict, since the court itself is not well versed in those customs and traditions.</p>
<ul>
<li>In the absence of such expert testimony, there can only be one conclusion: such claim remains unproved.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="settlement">Settlement<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#settlement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>In matters of civil litigation, parties can freely decide to settle their disputes out of court without court approval.</li>
<li>However, the court may intervene where the matter is already before it and grant approval to settle the matter out of court.</li>
<li>Where an agreement is reached, a consent will be filed to reflect the agreement and the court will record a consent judgment in order to close the matter.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="01">01<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#01" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The Kenyan justice system greatly encourages parties to address themselves to the principle of settling matters out of court because doing so will deliver justice in the shortest time possible so allowing parties to move on with their lives there after.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It also becomes expensive when parties decide to litigate, as this attracts court fees as well as advocates’ charges.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="confidentiality">Confidentiality<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#confidentiality" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>As long as the matter is first taken to court, then the parties decide to settle out of court, such settlement will remain on record because they first addressed their grievances through the courts.</li>
<li>Accordingly, a settlement cannot remain confidential as it forms part of the court record.</li>
<li>The parties may decide to leave out the details of the consent by merely marking the matter as settled.</li>
<li>Such consent is adopted as a court order and the details of settlement remain confidential.</li>
</ul>
<p>LECTURE 19: JUDGMENT AND DECREE</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="culmination-of-trial">CULMINATION OF TRIAL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#culmination-of-trial" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="what-is-a-judgment">What is a judgment?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-a-judgment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>After hearing is completed, the court will pronounce judgment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>O21 r1-6 deals with judgment and r.7-19 deals with decrees</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A Judgment is a final decision of the court on the facts of the case at the end of the entire procedure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The distinction between a judgment and an order is that the former is a final decision in an action, while the latter is an interlocutory decision, though it may have the effect of ending the action</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A judgment which determines the principal matter in question is final</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Such a judgment is obtained in all action by which a previously existing liability of the defendant to the plaintiff is ascertained or established</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Also such judgment can be obtained in an action by which the question whether there was a pre-existing right of the plaintiff against the defendant is finally determined in favour of either of the plaintiff or of the defendant</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A judgment or an order which does not deal with the final rights of the parties, but either is made before judgment and gives no final decision on the matters in dispute, but is merely on matter of procedure or is made after judgment and merely directs how the declarations of rights already given in the judgment are to be worked out is known as an Interlocutory Judgment</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tests-of-ascertaining-finality-of-a-judgment">Tests of ascertaining finality of a judgment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tests-of-ascertaining-finality-of-a-judgment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Was the order upon an application such that a decision in favour of either party would determine the main dispute?</li>
<li>Was it made upon an application upon which the main dispute could have been decided?</li>
<li>Does the order made, determine the dispute?</li>
<li>If the order in question is reversed would the action have to go on?</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ex-parte-judgment">Ex parte Judgment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ex-parte-judgment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>An ex parte judgment obtained by default of defence is by its nature not a judgment on merit and it is only entered because the party concerned has failed to comply with certain requirements of law</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The court has power to revoke such judgment, which is not pronounced on merit of the case or by consent but entered especially on failure to follow the requirement of the law</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="consent-judgment">Consent judgment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#consent-judgment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Where either party is willing to consent to a judgment or order against them, or</li>
<li>Where both parties are agreeable as to what the judgment or order ought to be, due effect may be given by the court to such a consent</li>
<li>A consent judgment derives its legal effect from the agreement of the parties</li>
<li>It is governed by the ordinary principles of contract and therefore can only be set aside in circumstances that afford a good ground for varying or rescinding a contract between parties</li>
</ul>
<p>A consent judgment can act as an estoppel which can be raised if fresh proceedings are brought alleging matters that are encompassed by the compromise</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Where the plaintiff has obtained judgment irregularly, the defendant is entitled ex debito justitiae to have such judgment set aside</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Persons authorized by the court to defend an action on behalf of others having the same interest cannot consent to the judgment against them – therefore, a next friend or guardian ad litem of an infant or person of unsound mind cannot consent without approval of the court</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A consent judgment cannot be set aside unless it can be shown that the same was obtained without instructions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Even if he has no specific instructions to enter a consent agreement and counsel only has general instructions, it is deemed they have full conduct of the matter and the apparent authority to compromise all matters connected with the action</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="who-makes-the-judgment">Who makes the judgment?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#who-makes-the-judgment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>As a general rule, the judge who heard the matter must make a judgment and such judge shall read the judgment</li>
<li>It must be read in open court</li>
<li>In certain circumstances, any judge may pronounce judgment, written and signed but not pronounced</li>
<li>Judgment should be signed</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="forms-and-contents-of-judgment">Forms and contents of judgment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#forms-and-contents-of-judgment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>(i) a judgmentary or introductory part, showing:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>(i) the form of the application upon which it was made</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>(ii) the parties appearing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>(iii) any consents, waivers, undertakings or admissions given or made, so placed as to indicate whether they relate to the whole judgment or only part thereof</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>(iv) a reference to the evidence judgment is made</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A substantive or mandatory part, containing:
(i) the order made by court
(ii) declaration of rights
(iii) consequential direction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Judgment in defended suits shall contain:
(a) a concise statement of the case
(b) the points of determination
(c) the decision thereon
(d) the reason for such decision</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When writing a judgment, it is important that</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>One ensures there are no irregularities;</li>
<li>Judgement should not be vague and certain points should not be left to inference;</li>
<li>It must be made of points raised in the pleadings in the course of trial; and</li>
<li>It must record all points raised by all parties.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The statement of facts recorded in the judgment will be the conclusive facts of the case</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All judicial pronouncements must be judicial in nature, sober, moderate and language must be used in a restrained and dignified manner</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Once a judgement has been read, the court becomes functus officio.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Under provisions of Section 99 for purposes of correcting clerical or arithmetical errors or errors arising from an accidental slip or omission the judgment may at any time be corrected by the court on its own motion or through an application of any party</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>O.21 requires that judgment be pronounced in open court either at once or within 60 days from the conclusion of the trial, notice of which shall be given to the parties or their advocates.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where judgment has not been given within 60 days, reasons thereof must be forwarded to the Chief Justice and a date of judgment immediately fixed (r.1)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Judgment must be dated and signed, and normally it will be read and signed by the person who wrote it (r.2(1))</p>
<ul>
<li>A judge is empowered to pronounce a judgment which has been written and signed but not pronounced by a predecessor (r.2(2))</li>
<li>It should be dated and signed by him in open court at the time of pronouncing it.</li>
<li>Where the judgment is read by a different judge who did not write the judgement the one who reads it should date and countersign it upon reading it (r.3(2))</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>In suits in which issues have been framed, the court shall state its finding or decision, with the reasons thereof, upon each separate issue (r.5)</p>
<ul>
<li>Where there is a prayer for judgment the grant of which would result in an alteration to the title of land registered under any written law concerning registered land, a certified copy of title shall be produced in court before judgment is delivered (r.6)</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="decree">Decree<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#decree" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A decree means a formal expression of an adjudication which so far as regards the court expressing it, conclusively determines the rights of the parties with regard to all or any of the matters in controversy in the suit and may be either preliminary or final</li>
<li>A decree is derived from the judgment and it must bear the date of the day on which the judgment was delivered</li>
<li>A successful party in a suit has a duty to extract a decree and submit it for approval of the other party – however failure to do so is not fatal</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Under Section 26 (1) of the Civil Procedure Act (Cap. 21, Laws of Kenya), where a decree is for the payment of money, the courts may in the decree order interest at such rate as is deemed reasonable to be paid on the principal sum, adjudged from the date of the suit to the date of the decree, in addition to any interest adjudged on such principal sum for any period before the institution of the suit to the date of the decree, in addition to any interest adjudged on such principal sum for any period before the institution of the suit, with further interest at such rate as the court deems reasonable on the aggregate sum so adjudged from the date of the decree to the date of payment, or to such earlier date as the court thinks fit.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="contents-of-a-decree">Contents of a Decree<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contents-of-a-decree" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A Decree is a technical translation of the judgment capable of execution.</li>
<li>In the High Court the parties themselves draw up the decree and take it back to court to be sealed.</li>
<li>The decree should be in agreement with the judgment.</li>
<li>The decree should contain the number of the suit, the names and descriptions of the parties, and particulars of the claim and shall specify the relief granted or other determination of the suit (r.7(1))</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The decree shall also state by whom or out of what property or in what proportion the costs incurred in the suit are to be paid (r.7(2))</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The court may direct that the costs payable to one party by the other shall be set-off against any sum which is admitted or found to be due from the former to the latter (r.7(3))</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A decree shall bear the date of the day on which the judgment was delivered (r.8(1))</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Any party to a suit in the High Court may prepare a decree and give it to the other party for approval, if the draft is approved by the parties, it shall be submitted to the registrar who if satisfied it is drawn up in accordance with the judgment shall sign and seal the decree and it becomes the official decree (r.8(2))</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>If one party does not receive an approval or rejection of the decree within 7 days, the party making it shall give notice in writing to that effect to the Registrar and if satisfied that the draft decree has been drafted in accordance with the judgment, shall sign and seal the decree accordingly</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>On any disagreement with the draft decree, any party may file the draft decree marked as “for settlement” and the Registrar shall list it in chambers before the judge who heard the case (or any other judge, if unavailable) and give notice to the parties (r.8(4))</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The procedure for preparation of decrees either in the High Court or Subordinate Courts is harmonised by importation of the current High Court procedure to subordinate courts (r.8(5))</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Any order, whether in the High Court or in a subordinate court, which is required to be drawn up, shall be prepared and signed in like manner as a decree (r.8(6))</p>
<ul>
<li>Where the amount of costs has been—</li>
</ul>
<p>(a) agreed between the parties;</p>
<p>(b) fixed by the judge or magistrate before the decree is drawn;</p>
<p>(c) certified by the Registrar under section 68A of the Advocates (Remuneration) Order; or</p>
<p>(d) taxed by the court,</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>the amount of costs may be stated in the decree or order (r.9(1))</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where the subject-matter of the suit is immovable property, the decree shall contain a description of such property sufficient to identify the same, and, where such property can be identified by boundaries or by numbers in a government record or survey, the decree shall specify such boundaries or numbers (r.10)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where the suit is in respect of movable property, and the decree is for the delivery of such property, the decree shall also state the amount of money to be paid as an alternative if delivery cannot be had (r.11)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Where it is a decree for payment of money, the court may for any sufficient reason at the time of passing the decree, order that payment be postponed or to be paid in instalments, with or without interest (r.12(1))</p>
<ul>
<li>Should the decree have been passed, the court may on application of the judgment-debtor and with or without permission of the decree-holder, with sufficient cause shown, order the payment of the amount decreed be postponed or made by instalments on such terms as payment of interest, attachment of property or taking of security from the judgment-debtor, as it thinks fit (r.12(2))</li>
</ul>
<p>If the suit is for the recovery of possession of immovable property and for rent or mesne profits, the court may pass a decree—</p>
<p>(a) for the possession of the property;</p>
<p>(b) for the rent or mesne profits which have accrued on the property before the institution of the suit or direct an inquiry as to the rent or mesne profits;</p>
<p>(c) directing an inquiry as to rent or mesne profits from the institution of such suit until—</p>
<p>(i) the delivery of possession to the decree-holder;</p>
<p>(ii) the relinquishment of possession by the judgment-debtor having notified the decree-holder through the court; or</p>
<p>(iii) the expiration of 3 years from the date of the decree, whichever event first occurs (r.13(1))</p>
<ul>
<li>Where an inquiry has been conducted a final decree in respect of the rent and mesne profits shall be passed in accordance with the result of the inquiry (r.13(2))</li>
</ul>
<p>If the decree made in the suit is for account or administration of property, the court shall pass a preliminary decree to order the accounts or inquiries to be taken or made (r.14(1))</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>While administering the property of a deceased person, if that property proves to be insufficient to pay of all his debts and liabilities, the decree-holders will be considered in terms of priority as secured and unsecured creditors as with respect to estates of persons declared insolvent</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Such persons will come in under the preliminary decree and make their claims (r.14(2))</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the decree made in the suit is for dissolution of a partnership, or the taking of partnership accounts, the court may before passing a final decree, pass a preliminary decree,
(i) declaring the proportionate shares of the parties,
(ii) fixing the day on which the partnership shall stand dissolved, or be deemed to have been dissolved, and
(iii) directing such accounts to be taken (r.15)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The special directions by the court with regard to taking account will involve the mode the account is to be taken and the court may direct while taking account that the books of account be taken as prima facie evidence of the truth of the matter therein contained</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The parties may object to this (r.17)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where a court passes a decree for the partition of property or for the separate possession of a share in it, the court may, if the partition or separation cannot be conveniently made without further inquiry, pass a preliminary decree declaring the rights of the parties interested in the property (r.18)</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Where the defendant has been allowed a set-off against the plaintiff’s claim, the decree shall state what amount is due to the plaintiff and what amount is due to the defendant, and shall be for the recovery of any sum which appears to be due to either party (r.19(1))</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The Registrar, or in the case of a subordinate court, the Presiding Magistrate shall upon written request by any of the parties or all of them, and upon payment of requisite fees, furnish certified copies of the judgment and decree:</p>
<ul>
<li>Nothing in this rule shall preclude the Registrar or the Presiding Magistrate from furnishing such copies to any person upon sufficient cause being shown for such request (r.20)</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>LECTURE 20: REMEDIES AFTER JUDMENT</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-to-stop-execution">HOW TO STOP EXECUTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-stop-execution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-stay-of-execution">1. Stay of Execution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-stay-of-execution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Every judgment or decree of a court of competent jurisdiction takes effect immediately upon pronouncement and every court has an inherent power to proceed to enforce such judgment or decree at once</li>
<li>However, the court has the power to stay execution if justice requires that the person against whom judgment is to be enforced should have this protection</li>
<li>The court has inherent jurisdiction over all judgments or orders that it made, under which it can stay in all cases</li>
</ul>
<p>O22 r5 states that:</p>
<p>Where a suit is pending in any court against the holder of a decree of such court in the name of the person against whom the decree was passed, the court may, on such terms as to security or otherwise, as it thinks fit, stay execution of the decree until the pending suit has been decided.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The court of appeal or the court below may stay execution pending an appeal, but mere service of notice of appeal does not operate as a stay (O42 r6(1))</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where the application for stay has not been granted, the party denied that order of stay may appeal to the appellate court against such order (O42 r6(1) and O22 r25)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The court of appeal may order a stay of execution of the judgment of a lower court, but before it does so, the lower court has inherent power to proceed to enforce its own judgment regardless of the fact that an appeal against judgment is pending before the court</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The only remedy to this is to apply for a stay of execution alongside an order to set aside judgment; one needs to base the application on the correct provisions of the civil procedure rules</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="grounds-for-application">Grounds for application<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#grounds-for-application" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The applicant will need to show that not only that the appeal has a real prospect of success, but:</li>
</ul>
<p>(i) the applicant stands to receive a substantial loss if the stay is not granted so as to render the appeal a nullity and the application has been made without unreasonable delay; and</p>
<p>(ii) the applicant has furnished such security as the court orders for due performance of such decree or order as may ultimately be binding on him (O42 r6(2))</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedure-of-stay-of-execution">Procedure of stay of execution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure-of-stay-of-execution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The application for stay may be made informally to the judge who decided the case when judgment is delivered (O42 r6(5))</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>And the court has the power to order such stay without a formal application, pending the hearing of the formal application for stay of execution (O42 r6(3))</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The application would be by way of notice of motion with the affidavit laying out the grounds for the application (O51 r1)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="automatic-stay-of-execution">Automatic stay of execution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#automatic-stay-of-execution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There are circumstances which have the effect of a stay:
(a) An order for the winding up of a company operates as a stay of execution on judgments against the company
(b) An order for an interpleader has an effect of a stay
(c) A garnishee order absolute made against a judgment-debtor and operates as a stay against the decree-holder, but a garnishee order obtained against a debt of the JD is not a stay against the JD so long as the garnishee has not paid under the order</li>
</ul>
<p>( d ) When a creditor who has obtained a judgment takes an order for payment in installments, he cannot afterwards issue execution</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Stay of execution only operates to prevent the DH from putting into operation the legal process of execution and does not affect any rights or remedies exercisable outside court</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The court has an absolute and unfettered discretion as to the granting or refusing a stay; and as to the terms upon which it will grant it</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The principle of law to be followed in application to stay execution is whether substantial loss would arise from not granting the same and whether the dictates of justice demand so</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When an order of the High Court to stay on terms has been passed and entered, subsequent variation of those terms can only be ordered by the Court of Appeal</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-payment-in-installments">2. Payment in installments<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-payment-in-installments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The JD may after the passing of judgment apply to the court with the consent of the DH, to pay the decretal sum in installments</li>
<li>An order for payment of installments after judgment and without consent of decree holder is a nullity</li>
<li>When an order for payment by installments has been made, there ceases to be a present for the whole amount of judgment debt, but a debt accruing by the amount of the installment per stipulated period and execution cannot issue in respect of the total amount remaining unpaid in the absence of any order to that effect</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="01">01<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#01" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A JD cannot bring an application asking the court to rescind its previous orders for payment by installment of a judgment debt nor for a new order to reduce the amount of the installments</li>
<li>It is only the DH who can move the court to rescind its previous order where it has come to his knowledge that the JD is in position to satisfy the judgment debt at once.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="objector-proceedings">Objector Proceedings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objector-proceedings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Upon execution by way of attachment of property, such attachment can be contested where the claimant or objector maintains that the property is not liable to such attachment as it is alleged it does not belong to the JD</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The power is extensive and it entails that any claim or objection raised must be investigated</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The rationale for this rule is to safeguard 3rd parties against improper and misconceived executions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Objector proceedings are in effect intended to enable holders of equitable interest to preserve their interest or entitlement in the absence of the legal or registered right e.g. bona fide occupants of land (O22 r51(1))</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A notice in writing containing the objection to the attachment of property is served upon the court, the JD and the DH (r51(1))</li>
<li>Notice to be accompanied by application supported by affidavit setting out in brief the nature of the claim which objector or claimant makes to the whole or portion of the property attached (r51(2))</li>
<li>Notice of objection and application to be served on all parties within 7 days of filing</li>
</ul>
<p>Upon receipt of a valid notice and application court may stay execution for not more than 14 days</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It shall then call upon the attaching creditor by notice in writing to intimate the court and all parties in writing within 7 days of whether it shall proceed with the attachment and execution of the said property, wholly or in part (r52)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Should the creditor not reply within the time stipulated in the court’s notice, or if they reply proposing that they do not intend to proceed with the attachment and execution of the said property, the court shall make an order raising the attachment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>And proceed to make an order as to costs (r53)</p>
</li>
<li></li>
<li>
<p>If the creditor proposes to proceed with attachment, the intimation shall be accompanied by a replying affidavit and the court shall proceed to hear the matter expeditiously (r54)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="what-is-to-be-investigated">What is to be investigated<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-to-be-investigated" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The question to be decided is:
(a) whether on the date of the attachment, the JD or objector was in possession
(b) where the court is satisfied that the property was in possession of the objector, whether he held it in his own account or in trust for the JD</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Therefore the sole question to be investigated is thus, one of possession</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Questions of legal right and title are not relevant, except insofar as they may affect the decision as to whether the possession is on account or in trust for the JD or some other person</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To that extent the title may be part of the inquiry</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The court is bound to order the release of the attached property if it finds that possession in the claimant on their own account, even if there is title and disposing power remaining in the JD</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The main basis of objection under this rule concerns possession, not title; and all objector must show is that he was in possession of the property at the time of attachment for property he claims an interest in</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The effect of objector proceedings if successful is to release the property from attachment</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>If it fails, the attachment proceeds as if it had not been challenged in the first place</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>However, if the issue of title is unresolved then a suit can be brought under r65 to countenance issues of title.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The objector does not appeal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The irregularity may not vitiate sale but any person sustaining an injury by reason of such irregularity at the hand of any other person may institute suit against him for compensation, recovery of specific property, as against the purchaser or compensation in default of recovery</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Objector proceedings must be brought promptly otherwise they fail if delay was deliberate or reckless</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There is no delay when there is no evidence that the person affected is aware of the date of attachment or the date of subsequent sale</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>LECTURE 21: EXECUTION OF DECREES AND ORDERS</p>
<p>HOW TO EXECUTE</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Execution in the widest sense signifies the enforcement of or giving effect to the judgment or orders of court of law</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Having obtained a judgment in his favour, the successful party may need to consider how such judgment can be enforced</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A court may on the application of the decree holder order execution of the decree:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>(a) by delivery of any property specifically decreed</p>
<p>(b) by attachment and sale or by sale without attachment, of any property</p>
<p>(c) by attachment of debts</p>
<p>(d) by arrest and detention in prison of any person</p>
<p>(e) by appointing a receiver</p>
<p>(f) in such other manner as the nature of the relief granted may require (s.38)</p>
<ul>
<li>It is the decree holder to select the appropriate means of execution of his decree, subject to the discretion of the court</li>
<li>Nothing prevent decree holder from applying for several modes of execution</li>
<li>But court may its discretion, refuse execution at the same time against the person and property of the judgment debtor</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="parties-to-execution">Parties to execution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#parties-to-execution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The person (decree holder) who is named or ascertained in a judgment or order is entitled to the benefit thereof and may issue execution against the person called the judgment debtor</li>
<li>Execution cannot issue against a non-party to the suit</li>
<li>However, where a person has become liable as a surety, then the decree or order may be executed against them to the extent to which they have rendered themselves personally liable</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The rights and liabilities of a JD may by reason of alienation, bankruptcy or death devolve upon some other person who may then issue, or be subject of a process of execution</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Every transferee of a decree shall hold the same subject to the equities, if any which the JD might have enforced against original DH</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In case the JD dies before the decree has been satisfied the holder of the decree may apply to court which passed it to execute the same against representative of such deceased or against such person who has intermeddled with estate of such deceased</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="which-court-executes-the-decree">Which court executes the decree?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#which-court-executes-the-decree" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>S.30 - The decree may be executed by the court that passed the decree or by the court to which it is sent for execution</li>
<li>S.31 Upon the application of the decree holder the court that passed the decree may send it to another court for execution.</li>
</ul>
<p>But there are four conditions that must be satisfied before this transfer is allowed:</p>
<p>(1) If the judgment debtor actually and voluntarily resides or carries on business or works for gain within the local limits of the jurisdiction of such other court.</p>
<p>(2) If the judgment debtor has no property within the local limits of the jurisdiction of the court which passed the decree.</p>
<p>(3) Where the decree directs the sale of immovable property situated outside the local limits of the jurisdiction of the court that passed the decree.</p>
<p>(4) Where the court that passed the decree considers for any other reason to be recorded that such other court should execute the decree.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="where-the-decree-is-sent-to-another-court-0-22-r-4">Where the decree is sent to another court 0.22 r.4<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#where-the-decree-is-sent-to-another-court-0-22-r-4" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Where the court sends decree for execution by another court, it should send-
(1) A copy of the decree;
(2) A certificate informing that satisfaction of the decree has not been obtained by execution within the jurisdiction of the court which passed it, or, where the decree has been executed in part, the extent to which satisfaction has been obtained and what part of the decree remains unexecuted; and
(3) A copy of any order for the execution of the decree, or, if no such order has been made, a certificate to that effect.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedure-for-execution">Procedure for execution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure-for-execution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Every application for execution shall be in writing (apart from an execution by way of arrest) signed and verified by the applicant and shall be in tabular form containing:
(i) suit number
(ii) parties
(iii) date of decree
(iv) whether appeal is preferred
(v) whether any part payment has been effected
(vi) whether there is previous application
(vii) amount due with interest, if any or other relief granted
(viii) amount of costs
(ix) name of person against whom execution is sought
(x) the mode in which assistance of the court is required</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="application-for-execution">Application for execution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#application-for-execution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>There must be formal application for execution; the court cannot execute a decree on its own motion. O.22 r.6 – a decree holder must apply for execution, there must be prompting by the decree holder</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the decree holder desires to execute, he must apply for execution either to the court that passed the decree or the court to which the decree is sent for execution. The application shall be as under Form 14 of Appendix A</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the judgment debtor fails to enter appearance or had entered appearance but failed to file a defence and a summary judgment is obtained then the court will not issue an execution order for payment, attachment or eviction, unless the judgment debtor is given at least 10 days notice of the fact that judgment has been entered against them</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This notice shall be attached to the first application of execution r.6</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Under r.7(1), in the case where the decree is for money payment, upon the oral application of the decree holder at the time of passing the decree they can ask for immediate execution by arresting the judgment debtor, especially if they are within the court precincts.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Otherwise every application for the execution of a decree should be made in writing signed by the applicant or his advocate stating that they require an execution order.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>And therein shall be contained in a tabular form the particulars under r.7(2)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>R.8 Where the attachment is of moveable property belonging to the judgement debtor but not in his possession, annexed to the decree holder’s application will be an inventory of the property to be attached with a reasonably accurate description of the moveable property.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>R.9 Where application is of immoveable property belonging to the judgement debtor it shall include:
(a) a description of the property sufficient to identify the same
(b) a specification of the judgment debtor’s share or interest in such property.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>R.10 If the immoveable property to be attached is registered in the land registry – the court may require the applicant to produce a certified extract from the register of such office indicating the person registered as proprietor or having interest in it.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>R.13 On receiving the application as under r.7(2) the court shall ascertain whether requirements under r.7-9 have been complied with, if not, it may reject the application or may allow it to be remedied there and then or within a stipulated time</li>
<li>R.13(4) when the application is admitted, the court shall order the execution according to the application.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="notice-to-show-cause-r-18">Notice to show cause r.18<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#notice-to-show-cause-r-18" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Where an application for execution is made:
(a) more than a year after the decree was made
(b) against the legal representative of the party to the decree
(c) for attachment of salary or allowance of any person;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>the court executing the decree shall issue a notice to the person against whom the decree has been issued requiring him to show cause, on a date to be fixed, why the decree should not be executed against him</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>R.19 Where the person who has been issued such notice does not appear or does not show sufficient cause as required by the court, the court shall order the decree to be executed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In certain cases before the execution can proceed, notice must be given to the JD to show cause why one should not proceed with execution;</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>a) where the decree is attached to the salary of the JD there must be notice to the JD to show cause why the decree should not be executed against him or her (r. 18);</p>
<p>b) why one should not be committed to civil jail (r.31)</p>
