<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="arrest-and-detention-s-40">Arrest and detention s.40<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#arrest-and-detention-s-40" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There is no provision that one must show cause but in reality one must issue notice to show cause unless the JD is within the precincts and an oral application has been made.</li>
</ul>
<p>Note:</p>
<ul>
<li>The decisions in:
(a) Rachael Mwikali Mwandia v. Ken Maweu Kasinga; and
(b) Sonia Kwamboka Rasugu v. Sandalwood Hotel &amp; Resort T/A Paradise Beach Resort &amp; Anor</li>
<li>have changed the rules with regard arrest and detention</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="why-should-notice-to-show-cause-be-issued-and-when">Why should notice to show cause be issued and when?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-should-notice-to-show-cause-be-issued-and-when" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Change of circumstances, e.g., where the JD is declared bankrupt, then circumstances would change; the capacity of the JD would have changed and a decree cannot be executed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where the JD dies or is not in existence in the case of a company.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Is under receivership</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The circumstances dictate that one must issue notice to show cause.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Where the notice to show cause is issued against the representatives of the JD, one must issue a notice to establish who the personal representative is and if whether the personal representative is available.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where the decree is for the attachment of the salary of the JD, notice must be issued since the JD could have been sacked or has quit. The notice is to establish whether the JD is still in employment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where execution is by way of attachment of salary, then the amount attached shall not exceed one third of the salary $.44</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The discretion to dispense with notice to show cause is vested with the court itself and therefore the Registrar has no power to dispense with the notice.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where there is requirement that a notice to show cause be issued and no notice is given, then any orders which the court may make in the absence of the JD are a nullity (Madhaji v Alibhai [1960] EA 167)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="process-of-execution">Process of execution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#process-of-execution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>R.20 Where the preliminary requirements required by the rules have been taken, the court shall issue its process for the execution of the decree.</li>
<li>Every process shall bear the date and day it was issued and signed by the judge and shall be sealed with the seal of the court and delivered to the proper officer to be executed (r.20(2)).</li>
<li>R.21 The officer entrusted with the execution of the process shall endorse on it the day and the manner it was executed, and if the last day specified in the process for the return of the process has been exceeded, the reason why it was not executed and shall return the process to the court with such endorsement to the court.</li>
</ul>
<p>Where the endorsement is about the officer’s inability to execute the process, the court may examine him and summon and examine witnesses as to that inability and record the results r.21(1)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>R.22 – provides for situations where the court to which the decree has been sent upon sufficient cause being shown stays execution to allow the JD to appeal to the court which passed the decree to set it aside or to go on appeal to an appellate court for a stay of execution.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where the JD’s property had been seized on execution, the court issuing the execution orders may order restitution of property or his discharge r.22(2)</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>The court may require security from or impose conditions on JD before ordering for stay of execution, restitution of his property or his discharge r.22(3)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The proper application for stay of execution should be made under O.42 r.6 –</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>One can proceed under r.7(2) - which gives one the authority to invoke the court of appeal jurisdiction.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>One must first apply to the High Court under O.42 r6, when the stay is rejected, one can go straight to court of appeal under rule 7(2) to invoke the court of appeal jurisdiction to grant the stay.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The second attempt to the court of appeal should be under O.42 r.6(1) which is an appeal but going under r.7(2) is when one has not appealed the order in the high court but is going straight to the Court of Appeal.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
<li>
<p>R.24 Any order of the court by which a decree is passed or of the appellate court in relation to execution of the decree shall be binding upon the court to which the decree is sent for execution</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="execution-on-cross-decrees">Execution on cross decrees<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#execution-on-cross-decrees" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="r-14">r_14<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#r-14" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is where each party has a decree against the other. This can only occur where the following conditions exist</p>
<ol>
<li>The same court receives applications for executions of the cross decrees</li>
<li>Each decree is for payment of money</li>
<li>Both decrees are capable of execution at the same time and by the same court.</li>
<li>The parties have filed the suit in the same capacity of character in the same cases.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>If those conditions are satisfied, then the court must record that they are satisfied and that the sums are equal.</li>
<li>If the sums are not equal, then the one with the larger sum will be allowed to execute.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="decree-for-payment-of-money">Decree for payment of money<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#decree-for-payment-of-money" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>F 26 decree for payment of money may be executed by detention in prison of the judgment debtor or attachment of his property, or both.</p>
<ul>
<li>S.38 Execution by detention in prison shall not be ordered unless after giving JD an opportunity to show cause why he should not be committed to prison the court, for reasons recorded in writing, is satisfied –</li>
</ul>
<p>(a) JD with object of obstructing or delaying execution
(i) is likely to abscond or leave local limits
(ii) has after institution of the suit in which decree is passed, dishonestly transferred, concealed or removed any part of his property, or committed any other act in bad faith in relation to his property
(b) That the JD has, or has had since the date of the decree, the means to pay the amount of the decree, or some substantial part of it, but refuses or neglects to pay the same.
(c) Decree was for a sum for which the JD was in a fiduciary capacity to account for.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="decree-for-specific-moveable-property-r-27">Decree for specific moveable property r.27<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#decree-for-specific-moveable-property-r-27" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Where the decree is for a specific moveable or for any share in a specific moveable property, it may be executed by the seizure, where practicable, of the moveable property or share, and delivery of it to the party to whom it has been adjudged, or by arrest and detention of the JD, or attachment of his property or both.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>R.27(2) Where attachment has remained in force for 6 months, if the JD has not obeyed the decree and the DH has applied for the attached property to be sold, it may be sold and the proceeds of sale awarded to the DH</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Execution depends on the subject matter.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In the case of movable property, for example, normally you will execute by delivering to the person it has been granted, and therefore it will be executed by seizing and delivering that property.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Suppose the judgment debtor refuses to release that property: you can have them arrested.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sometimes you can merely attach the property, e.g. a vehicle by notifying the Registrar of Motor Vehicles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This power can only be used where the property is under the possession of the judgment debtor or his agent.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="what-about-immovable-property">What about immovable property?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-about-immovable-property" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Usually you can execute by removing the judgment debtor from that property and putting the decree holder in possession.</li>
<li>Sometimes delivery of property can be <strong>symbolic</strong>. It does not always have to be physical and actual possession.</li>
<li>For both movable and immovable property, you can attach and sell, where the execution order empowers the decree holder the power to attach and sell the property.</li>
<li>An order allowing attachment is different from an order of sale, unless you apply for both at the same time.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="attachment-0-22-r-36-50">Attachment 0.22 r.36-50<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#attachment-0-22-r-36-50" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Attachment of immovable property</li>
<li>Where the property to be attached is agricultural produce, you attach the property by affixing a warrant of attachment in the field where the property is growing or where it is stored or where the JD resides or works for gain.</li>
<li>If it involves share of dividend in a company issue a prohibitory order against the person in whose name the share is registered.</li>
<li>The Order prohibits the transfer of the share or receipt of any dividend on that share.</li>
</ul>
<p>If the property is moveable in possession of a 3rd Party, attachment is with prohibition order against 3rd party.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Immoveable property – attachment is by registering a prohibitory order against JD in whose name the property is registered.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The order prohibits the JD from transferring, charging the property in any way and prohibits 3rd parties from transferring the property, the order is against the JD or any party with an interest.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The attachment against immoveable property becomes complete and effective when a copy of the prohibitory order is registered against the title.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>Attachment of Salary – firstly one has to issue a notice to show cause served on the JD and if the JD does not show sufficient cause, then the court will make an order attaching one third of the salary of the JD and the order will require that the employer deducts one third of the salary and forfeits to the court or the advocate of the Decree Holder if the court so directs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The reasoning is that one third is what a person saves and therefore can afford.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Sale of immovable property</li>
<li>The procedure of selling immovable property is lengthy and complex and one has to abide by it. When one wants to attach immovable property one has to register the prohibitory order to ensure that JD and third parties do not interfere with the property.</li>
<li>Then one has to actualize the sale.</li>
</ul>
<p>Establish if there are third parties with an interest in that property like a financial institution, the interest must be noted and catered for by fixing the matter with deputy registrar for settlement of terms of sale to establish value of property and what other parties have interest in the property and how the interests can be catered for and when and how the property will be sold.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The court will then give an indication on how the property is to be sold subject to a reserve price. The court may also wants to find out how much is owed and then it may direct that after the sale the third party interests be catered for and the net sum is what will be available in settling the debt.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If there is a charge registered against the title, the same may be discharged if the court directs and if the chargee is holding the title they must release title to facilitate transfer.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sale">Sale<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sale" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>O.22 states sale can only be conducted by public sale, by an officer (auctioneer) appointed by the court.</li>
<li>A public notice to advertise the intended sale must be posted and the court can direct the manner in which the sale will be directed in giving the order.</li>
<li>Usually public notice and advertisements should be done by decree holder and after the judgment debtor have been notified.</li>
<li>Notice should state date and time and place of sale, and usually the amount that is intended to be recovered or the encumbrance of the property, and any other information that is material as directed by the court.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>The notice should be at least 30 days in the case of immovable property and 15 days in the case of movable property.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>These time periods can be changed if the goods are perishable or subject to decay.</li>
<li>The court still has the discretion to adjourn the sale and usually the officers in charge of the sale will be served with notice.</li>
<li>If adjourned by more than 7 days a fresh public notice must be given.</li>
</ul>
<p>Once the property is sold the proceeds of sale are paid to the decree holder or his advocate and if there is any balance, it is paid over to the JD.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Every sale is usually conducted by an officer appointed by court, by way of public auction.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The court attaches a public notice of intended sale to be carried in such a manner as it may direct and the court will give notice to decree holder and JD indicating the date, the time and the place of intended sale by auction and it should also specify as accurately as possible the property to be sold, any encumbrance to which the property is subject, amount to be recovered after the sale and any other matter which the court considers material for purchaser to know in order to assess the nature and value of the property.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
<li>
<p>Except with the consent in writing of the JD, the sale will not take place until after expiry of at least 30 days in the case of immoveable property and at least 15 days in the case of moveable property.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This period is calculated from the date in which the copies of the notices are affixed on the court notices.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where the property is subject to speedy and natural decay (inherent vice) then the officer tending to the auction may sell it at once.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If it is livestock the court may make arrangements for its custody and maintenance i.e. the court directs that it may be held at the nearest prison since there are fields and free labour.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The court has the discretion to adjourn the sale to a specified date and hour and an officer conducting any such sale may also adjourn it giving the reasons for adjournment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the sale is to be conducted in presence of the court it cannot be adjourned without the leave of court.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If adjourned for more than 7 days a fresh date must be given</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Every sale shall be stopped if before the sale is completed:</li>
</ul>
<p>(1) The outstanding debt and cost has been paid by the debtor to the presiding officer</p>
<p>(2) Proof is given to the officer that the amount of debt and costs has been paid to the court which ordered the sale i.e. by production of a receipt.</p>
<p>The Decree holder must not participate at the auction without the permission of the court and if he participates directly or through another person, the court may set aside that sale and the court may set aside the sale if the JD applies or if any other person whose interests have been affected by the sale applies to the court.</p>
<ul>
<li>If it turns out that there was improper sale, the cost of that sale and proceedings will be borne by the decree holder.</li>
<li>If after auctioning the proceeds are not enough to satisfy the decree, then the decree holder can look for any other property that the JD may have if the warrants are still valid, one need not make a fresh application.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="appointment-of-receiver">Appointment of receiver<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#appointment-of-receiver" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>You can also execute by appointment of receivers.</li>
<li>You appoint receivers as an interim measure or as a mode of execution.</li>
</ul>
<p>LECTURE 21 A: ATTACHMENT OF DEBTS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="garnishee-proceedings">GARNISHEE PROCEEDINGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#garnishee-proceedings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>0.23</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="01">01<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#01" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Attachment of debts is a process by means of which a decree holder is enabled to reach money due to the judgment debtor, which is in the hands of a third person</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To support a garnishee there must be a debt due or accruing due, it is not sufficient to show a contingent liability</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This is a convenient method of executing against a judgment debtor since the money is intercepted on its way to them before it comes within their possession</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The third person in whose hands the money is, which is sought to be attached is called the garnishee, the requisite proceeds are known as garnishee proceedings and the necessary order is called a garnishee order</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The garnishee order changes the obligation from paying a judgment debtor to paying the decree holder</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="garnishee-when-instituted">Garnishee when instituted<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#garnishee-when-instituted" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The proceedings are instituted by a person who has obtained a judgment or order for recovery of payment of money by an assignee of judgment debt or by representatives of a deceased decree holder who have been parties to the action in which judgment or order in question has been given or made</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The test as to whether debt is attachable is whether it is owing by garnishee and it is the type of debt which the judgment debtor can enforce against</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Such debt must be in existence at the date when the attachment becomes operative, something that the law recognizes as a debt and not something that may or ,may not become a debt</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Thus, when the existence of a debt depends upon the performance of a condition, there is no attachable debt until the condition has been duly performed</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Where an existing debt is payable by future installments, the garnishee order may be made to become operative as and when each installment becomes due</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Money in hands of a bank is always attachable by garnishee and the bank has to show whether order nisi should not be made absolute by claiming a lien over the money in its possession</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Until the garnishee admits his indebtness to the judgment debtor, the garnishee order nisi cannot be meaningfully made absolute</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The existence and availability of funds belonging to judgment debtor has to be conclusively established as a condition precedent to making the order absolute</p>
</li>
<li></li>
<li>
<p>Although a banker has a general lien on all securities deposited with it by a customer unless there is an express contract or circumstance, which is inconsistent with it, money is usually not the subject of a lien as it is not capable of being earmarked.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The banker’s claim in such cases would probably be more rightly referred to as set off</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedure-0-23">Procedure 0.23<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure-0-23" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Application is made <em>ex parte</em> with a supporting affidavit which must state:</li>
</ul>
<p>(i) the name and address of the judgment debtor,</p>
<p>(ii) identify the judgment to be enforced, giving the amount remaining unpaid,</p>
<p>(iii) state to the best of information or belief of deponent the garnishee is within the jurisdiction and is indebted to the JD, and</p>
<p>(iv) if the garnishee is a deposit taking institution having more than one place of business, give the name and address of the branch at which JD’s account is believed to be held, the number of account</p>
<p>(v) and if all or part of this information is not known to deponent, the fact it is not known</p>
<ul>
<li>The order upon application may be made either or after the oral examination of the JD</li>
<li>Order may be that such debts owing to JD be attached to answer the decree including costs of garnishee proceedings</li>
<li>That order or a subsequent order can order the garnishee to appear before court to show cause why he should not pay to the DH the debt due from them to the JD (O.23 r.1(1))</li>
<li>7 days before hearing of application, order nisi shall be served upon garnishee and JD</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="effect-of-order">Effect of order<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effect-of-order" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>From the date of service on the garnishee the order attaching any debt due or accruing due from the garnishee to the debtor, or so much as is sufficient to satisfy the claim of the DH against the debtor, including costs, entered an order to show cause</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Until service of order nisi, there is no attachment of the debt</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the garnishee bona fide pays to JD the amount of debt before service, the order nisi is absolute as there is no longer any debt to which it can attach</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where garnishee has paid JD by cheque before the service of the order nisi, he is under no obligation to stop the cheque</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the cheque is stopped or dishonoured, the attachment will operate</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The service of order nisi creates an equitable charge and the garnishee cannot pay the debt to anybody without incurring the risk of having to pay it again</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="order-absolute">Order absolute<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#order-absolute" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The court has discretion as to whether order should be made absolute</li>
<li>The court must have regard to the position of the other creditors so far as they are known by the court</li>
<li>The court must be satisfied before it makes an order absolute that there is a debt in praesenti</li>
<li>A garnishee order will place the DH in the same position as an assignee of the JD and will make him subject to the equities, which exist against debtor</li>
<li>Garnishee may also obtain execution if the money is not paid in accordance with the order absolute</li>
</ul>
<p>Any payment made by the garnishee in compliance with an order absolute and any execution levied against them in pursuance of the order is deemed to be a valid discharge of the liability of the garnishee personally in the proceedings</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Cost awarded against garnishee where the proceedings are improperly defended are not to be counted in the discharge of the liability of the garnishee</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Payment by the garnishee made under the order absolute will discharge any obligation to pay debt to debenture holders under a floating charge that has not crystallized before payment</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="01">01<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#01" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>However, were DH has not yet received payment under a garnishee order absolute, a receiver appointed for debenture holder will obtain priority over the garnishee order</li>
<li>Where the court refuses to make the order absolute, it will direct order nisi to be discharged</li>
<li>A garnishee order may be set aside where there is a mistake of fact</li>
</ul>
<p>LECTURE 21B: EXECUTION AGAINST GOVERNMENT</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="special-procedure-for-enforcement-of-judgments-against-government">SPECIAL PROCEDURE FOR ENFORCEMENT OF JUDGMENTS AGAINST GOVERNMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#special-procedure-for-enforcement-of-judgments-against-government" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>No order against the government may issue under:
(a) Order 14, rule 4 (Impounding of documents);
(b) Order 22 (Execution of decrees and orders);
(c) Order 23 (Attachment of debts);
(d) Order 40 (Injunctions); and
(e) Order 41 (Appointment of receiver). (O29 r2(2))</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>An application for a certificate (Certificate of Satisfaction Order) under section 21 of the Government Proceedings Act (which relates to satisfaction of orders against the Government) shall be made to a registrar or, in the case of a subordinate court, to the court;</li>
<li>Any application under that section for a direction that a separate certificate be issued with respect to costs ordered to be paid to the applicant shall be made to the court</li>
<li>and may be made ex parte without a summons, and such certificate shall be in one of Form Nos. 22 and 23 of Appendix A (O29 r3)</li>
</ul>
<p>The copy of Certificate of Satisfaction Order accompanied by the judgment is served on the Accounting Officer, after endorsement by the Attorney General, by the decree holder</p>
<ul>
<li>The certificate has to state the amount payable plus interest thereon</li>
<li>The decree holder could obtain payment by the Attorney General writing to the proper accounts office instructing him to effect payment</li>
<li>Where the official refuses to pay, the judgment debtor can apply for an order of mandamus</li>
<li>The High Court through this order which is directed to the public officer in question requiring him to do that for which he is under a public duty to do</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>When leave has been granted to apply for an order of mandamus, the application shall be made within 21 days by notice of motion to the High Court</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There shall be at least 8 clear days between the service of the notice of motion and the day named therein for the hearing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The notice shall be served on all persons directly affected, including the AG and the Accounting Officer</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An affidavit of service will be necessary to show notification of concerned parties</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In case an order of mandamus is granted and such officer is still obstinate, court can invoke contempt of court proceedings, or</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>by application for notice to show cause why the respondent should not be committed to a civil prison for non-compliance with order of mandamus</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Republic v Permanent Secretary Office Of The President Ministry Of Internal Security &amp; another ex-parte Nassir Mwandihi [2014] eKLR (Miscellaneous Civil Application JR 132 of 2010)</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div data-testid="stAppIframeResizerAnchor" data-iframe-height="true" class="st-emotion-cache-1dumvfu eht7o1d9"></div></section></div></div></div><div data-testid="portal" id="portal" class="st-emotion-cache-1q6lfs0 e19n7mk11"></div></div><div class=""></div></div>
